Local News

Zhenru International Radio Station Held Opening Ceremony Yesterday

More Than 2,000 Guests Attended

More Than a Dozen Congratulatory Telegrams Received

Broadcasting Began in the Morning

The International Radio Station built by the Ministry of Transportation in Zhenru held its opening ceremony yesterday. More than 2,000 representatives and guests attended. The opening ceremony began at 2:00 PM to the sound of military music, presided over by Minister of Transportation Wang Boqun and with Lu Guixiang as the master of ceremonies. The ceremony concluded at 5:00 PM. The details of the event are recorded below:

A Glimpse of the Radio Station The site is located north of Zhenru Station, in front of Jinwang Temple, covering an area of over 191 mu. A small river runs west of the station. The layout of the radio station is very beautiful. There are two sections of machinery, with the power generation room in the middle. Behind the power generation room is the Sino-French radio station, and to the east is the Sino-American and Sino-German radio station. In the center is a reservoir, surrounded by stone streets. Yesterday's venue was built on the west side of the radio station, using temporary reed sheds that could accommodate thousands of people. Two wireless radio amplifiers were placed in the venue, so the sound was very clear during the speeches.

Venue Arrangement Yesterday afternoon, participating guests gathered at the North Station. At 1:00 PM, a special train began to depart, arriving at Zhenru Station. Reception staff had prepared six cars to transport guests back and forth to the radio station's temporary venue. More than a hundred city public security bureau box gun teams and machine gun teams were stationed around the venue, guarding the streets. Soon, Boqun, Zhangqun, Wang Zhengting, and others arrived in succession, and the meeting began immediately. The station's reception staff distributed a copy of the radio station's work report to each guest. After the meeting, the special train returned guests to Shanghai. By the time they arrived in the city, the lights of thousands of homes were already lit.

Attending Representatives Yesterday, many representatives and guests attended, including representatives from the National Government and the Executive Yuan: Zhangqun; representatives from the Central Party Headquarters: Wu Daoyi; Minister of Transportation: Wang Boqun; Foreign Minister: Wang Zhengting; Director of the Telecommunications Administration: Liang Zhuang Zhihuan; Director of the Wireless Radio Administration: Wen Yuqing; Director of the Shanghai Telephone Bureau: Zhao Shouheng; Director of the Arsenal: Guo Chengen; Lin Kanghou from the Bankers' Association; Chen Zheqing; Ye Huijun from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce; Wang Xiaolai; Jiang Weizu and Yang Sili from the Postal Administration; Wang Zhiwei from the Telecommunications School; Lu Guixiang, Director of the Electrical Machinery Factory; Tang Hongsheng from the Public Concession Police Department; Chen Bichang and Lin Xiangzhong from the Wireless Radio Station of the Second Brigade of the Marine Corps; Sun Jingxi and Wang Yiwu from the Zhongfu Bank; Tang Baoshu, the Shanghai Branch Manager of the Hong Kong National Bank; Huang Huannan, Supervisor of the Sincere Company, and more than 2,000 others. On the foreign side, there were French Consul General: Gamglin; German Vice Consul: Tang Shili; Bai Luobao, Import Manager of the American Most Company; Hansen, General Manager of Siemens; Zhai Na from the German Telefunken Wireless Radio Company; Ma En, Manager of the Asian Commander Company; and Hasenna, Manager of the Zen Chen Company, forty or fifty people in total.

Venue Staff Chairman: Wang Boqun; Master of Ceremonies: Lu Hongxun, Section Chief of the Wireless Radio Administration; Zhuang Zhihuan, Director of the Telecommunications Administration; Chen Danshi, Section Chief of the Fifth Section of the Telecommunications Administration; and various section chiefs of the Administration and engineers from the Preparatory Office were responsible for reception.

Opening Ceremony Order (1) Opening of the Meeting (2) Bowing Three Times to the National Flag, Party Flag, and Portrait of Dr. Sun Yat-sen (3) The Chairman Respectfully Reads Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Will (4) Playing of Music (5) Unveiling Ceremony (6) The Chairman Reports on the Preparations and Establishment Process (7) Speech by the Central Representative (8) Speech by the National Government Representative (9) Speeches by Guests (10) Chairman's Response (11) Playing of Music (12) Photography (13) Refreshments (14)

Adjournment

Unveiling Ceremony After performing the rituals, the unveiling ceremony was held. Minister Wang Boqun presented the keys to the two electric power rooms to Zhang Chengju, the engineering director of the International Radio Station Preparatory Office. Zhang then used the keys to open the Sino-US and Sino-German electric power rooms, followed by the Sino-French electric power room. The unveiling ceremony was then completed.

Speeches from All Parties Initially, Chairman and Minister Wang Boqun delivered a speech. Then, Wu Daoyi, the representative of the Central Party Headquarters, and Zhangqun, the representative of the National Government, gave instructions. Among the guests who spoke were Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting, Ye Huijun, the representative of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Gamglin, the French Consul General representing the French government, Neng Si, the Far East Manager of the American Wireless Radio Company, and Li Bai, the General Representative of the American Wireless Radio Company, who gave speeches of congratulations. Finally, Minister Wang Boqun gave a response. Afterwards, Wang led the guests to visit the various rooms.

Minister Wang's Speech The meeting began at 2:00 PM. First, the Chairman gave a speech, saying, "Today is the opening of the International Radio Station. I am grateful that the Central Party Headquarters and the National Government have sent personnel to guide us, and that representatives from various ministries and departments and people from all walks of life, both Chinese and foreign, have been willing to come. This not only adds infinite glory to our opening ceremony, but also increases our spirit of enterprise immeasurably. In addition to our joy, we must thank you all. The International Radio Station is just one item in our material construction, but there are several reasons why we have rushed to prepare the International Radio Station. First, it is to meet the needs of the nation and the people, because the international telecommunications industry is not only a hub for international transportation, but also often a place where the national spirit is entrusted. Since our country's unification, its international standing has been increasing day by day, and with the gradual abolition of unequal treaties, agriculture, industry, and commerce have been developing. The relationship between our country and the people in the international community has also become more complex. The International Radio Station is both a means of transportation and a place where the national spirit is often entrusted. It must be completed as soon as possible to meet future needs. Second, it is to protect the right to international communication. Our country's international telecommunications industry has been controlled by foreign merchants for about 50 years. Foreign control of telecommunications tools has not only hindered national rights, but also affected the progress of politics, diplomacy, and commerce, preventing it from making long-term progress. Now that the country is undergoing reform, we should actively abolish unequal treaties and work hard to build new industries such as international radio stations to protect national rights. Third, it is to promote international sentiment. In the past, due to the lack of international transportation, foreigners often had unclear observations of our country and often criticized us as mysterious or backward. In the future, with the development of transportation, their views on our country will gradually change. From this, it can be seen that transportation is closely related to international sentiment. Although I dare not say that the establishment of the Grand Radio Station will achieve any results in this regard, it will still be of some benefit. Fourth, it is to increase the effectiveness of international propaganda. Our country's international communications industry is still in its infancy. Whenever incidents occur involving foreign countries, they always rely on their transportation tools to obscure the facts and reverse black and white. This is especially true when tragic incidents have occurred over the years. Therefore, whenever the people of our country are extremely angry, they always hate the lack of international propaganda tools. Now that the Grand Radio Station has been established, this shortcoming should be slightly reduced. The above four points are the reasons why we are rushing to build the International Radio Station. As for whether we can achieve them, we still need the joint care of all the guests and the people of the country. Next, there are also things about the preparations for the International Grand Radio Station that can be reported to you. Last February, the Ministry sent personnel to prepare the International Wireless Radio Station and ordered machines from French merchants to set up a Sino-French radio station in Pudong, Shanghai. At the same time, the Construction Committee also ordered machines from Germany and the United States and prepared to build an international radio station in Zhenru Baoshan Liuhang and an international branch station in Fenglinqiao, Shanghai. Last August, the Ministry received the wireless radio business run by the Construction Committee and merged the two preparatory offices of the Ministry and the Committee to focus on completion and supervise employees to actively proceed. In March of this year, the Fenglinqiao International Branch Station was completed. In April, it communicated with the Philippines, Hong Kong, and the Dutch East Indies, and relayed communications with Europe and the United States from the Philippines. In November, the Grand Radio Station was fully completed and tested communication with San Francisco in the United States and Berlin in Germany with excellent results. From the start of the radio station's preparations to the present, it has taken one and a half years. The total construction cost is over 400,000 US dollars and about 540,000 in national currency. Although this project seems huge on the surface, after 1920, our country's international communications can be closely related to the world.

Mr. Wang Boqun, Chairman of the International Radio Station Opening Ceremony, Taken by Our Newspaper

We will no longer worry about any obstacles or rely solely on foreigners. The joy is shared by all the people of the country. The International Grand Radio Station is of great importance. Although it has been successfully completed, the matter is still in its early stages, and wireless radio often affects radio waves due to climate differences. In case it is not sensitive enough in future use, I hope that the people of the country will not destroy it in order to achieve perfection. However, the Ministry will always strictly supervise and manage it to ensure that no accidents occur in order to live up to the enthusiasm of the people of the country. I also hope that people in China will continue to provide guidance at any time so that this emerging industry will become more perfect and the world will directly and indirectly enjoy its benefits. This is not only an honor for colleagues in the transportation industry."

Speech by the Central Representative Wu Daoyi, the representative of the Central Party Headquarters, said in his speech, "Today is the opening day of the International Wireless Radio Station. From my personal point of view, although there are many issues related to the progress of the world, the development of the nation, and the promotion of civilization, many of them are related to transportation. Our country has not paid much attention to the transportation industry and has fallen behind others. The establishment of the International Radio Station is quite gratifying. The International Radio Station is like a person's throat and tongue. Without a radio station, it is like a person without a throat and tongue who cannot speak. In the past, our country did not have an International Wireless Radio Station, so we suffered a lot of losses in the international community. Through the International Radio Station, we can improve our country's commercial and political situation. Many countries in Europe, America, and Japan have established International Radio Stations. The radio station machinery is all manufactured by themselves, and they are constantly researching and making rapid progress. However, the structure and equipment of our country's radio stations all rely on foreigners. I am quite regretful about this. In the future, I hope that our people can build the second and third International Radio Stations themselves, which would be even more glorious."

Speech by the National Government Representative Zhangqun, the representative of the National Government and the Executive Yuan, said in his speech that the International Radio Station built by the Ministry of Transportation has been completed today. I think there are two major radio stations in Shanghai, and the address is only two or three minutes away from Shanghai. Whether it is in transportation or communication, it will be very convenient in all aspects. In fact, the Chinese and foreign citizens of Shanghai will also have many conveniences. The beginning of our country's telecommunications business was in the early years of the Qing Guangxu period. Today, it has been more than 50 years. However, all telegraphs have only two types: land lines and water lines. The establishment of telegraph offices is only in eight places: Shanghai, Wusong, Chongming, Guangzhou, Beiping, Tianjin, Hankou, and Harbin. The scale is very small, and it is very difficult to communicate with the international community. Even domestically, there are sometimes obstacles. At that time, there were only two international land lines: the Sino-Russian line and the Sino-French line. The Sino-Russian line ran from Zhangjiakou Chaketu through Siberia to our country. The Sino-French line ran from Vietnam through Annam to France. The sea lines included the Shanghai-Sasebo line and the Shanghai-Nanyang line. The above two lines passed through places such as Qingdao, Hong Kong, and Nagasaki. However, this type of business was entirely controlled by foreigners, such as the Great Northern and Great Eastern companies. Our country's economy was manipulated, and national rights were inevitably abandoned. However, this matter is related to unequal treaties, but it can really be said that we did not have our own construction. For example, we have been promoting domestic goods everywhere recently. Promoting domestic goods is a patriotic action. If everyone loves the country and the supply of domestic goods is not enough, then what will happen? This is very clear. Now that the International Radio Station has been completed, we will no longer have to borrow from foreigners. However, I hope that we will continue to work hard, on the one hand, to abolish unequal treaties, and on the other hand, not to think that having one radio station is enough. Only when we have international radio stations in the country can we be considered to have achieved construction."

Speech by the Guests Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting said in his speech that in my opinion, the degree of radio communications in the future is immeasurable. Foreigners have made more rapid progress in radio than our country. Our country does not use scientific methods, so the radio communications business cannot progress. The establishment of the International Radio Station is a good sign of the progress of the radio communications business. The only benefit of the radio station is that our country can speak for itself in the future without having to rely on foreigners. Nowadays, many foreigners do not understand what our country's country is like, what our nation is like, what our construction policy is, and what our political strategy is. The people of our country also do not understand the situation of foreign countries. Both sides feel isolated, and misunderstandings arise from time to time. In the future, we can use the transportation methods of radio stations to understand each other's claims and understand each other's situations. It can be seen that radio stations do have great benefits. In remote and blocked places such as Gansu, Xinjiang, Yunnan, and Guizhou, transportation is blocked, and it takes about ten days to receive a telegram. After the radio station is built, it can be reached quickly, and the people of the country can better understand the domestic situation. Only when the domestic situation is clear can we deal with foreign countries. Therefore, the use of radio stations is extremely great, and it is not only related to transportation. In addition, Ye Huijun also gave a speech (omitted). Foreign guests included the French Consul and others who gave speeches.

Speech by the French Consul General The French Consul General Gamglin said in his speech, "Foreign Minister Wang, ladies and gentlemen, the opening of the Chinese International Radio Station marks the complete independence of the new China's wireless communication with Europe. This move is extremely important. I am pleased to see that French expertise has helped the Chinese allies to develop this necessary product of a modern country. In recent years, although French experts have not tried to implement patent policies in China, they have assisted the National Government in the Chinese wireless radio business. The establishment of wireless radio communication between China and Europe is a great honor, and I am very satisfied with the assistance of French experts. On March 4, 1920, a contract was signed with the French Wireless Radio Company stating that wireless communication between China and Europe would be relayed by the French Saint-Étienne radio station. A 15-kilowatt shortwave transmitting station was set up in Zhenru, a receiving station was set up in Liuhang, and a wireless radio station was set up in the Sassoon building in Shanghai.

Panoramic View of the Zhenru International Wireless Radio Station (Taken by Ye Changlie)

The opening ceremony is for the above-mentioned places. The equipment is unseen in the East, such as the wireless radio frame and the camera, which are only available in major cities around the world. I would like to extend my congratulations to Minister Wang Boqun of the Ministry of Transportation, because Minister Wang has the courage to move forward without fear of setbacks, and that is why we have today's achievements. I would also like to extend my congratulations to my old friends, Zhuang Zhihuan, Director of the Telecommunications Department of the Ministry of Transportation, and Wen Yuqing, Director of the Wireless Radio Administration. When the three French experts were doing their best to help the Chinese government build its business, I would like to toast to Baski, the representative of the French Wireless Radio Company, who negotiated the contract in 1920, as well as Shawai, who built the project, and Gu Liwah, who calibrated all the programs in the radio station. I congratulate this business run by the Chinese and French, which is related to national progress and ethnic connections."

Wang Boqun's Response Briefly stated that Chen Meng and all walks of life came, and he was honored to receive congratulations from the National Government, the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. Although the wireless radio station was established this time, due to financial constraints, the various equipment was extremely simple, and safety equipment was not installed outside the ground. These are all shortcomings. I hope to do my best to improve it in the shortest possible time. After the National Government's finances are slightly more abundant, there should be a slightly more complete installation."

In addition to my congratulations, I am deeply confident that the friendly and beneficial cooperation granted by your government will continue forever, and I am deeply confident that the wireless communication business will achieve great success, because the two countries will be able to freely exchange their ideals and doctrines in the future.

Wen Yuqing's Reply to Winterbotham: I am honored to receive your congratulatory telegram on the occasion of the opening of the International Wireless Station. On behalf of my colleagues, I express my sincere thanks for your kind intentions and the cooperation provided by you and your colleagues. I deeply hope that through this direct wireless facility, not only can the relationship between the American Wireless Company and the National Government's Wireless Administration be closer, but also the bond between the people of the two countries can be more consolidated. Also, the General Manager of the German Telefunken Wireless Telegraph Company sent a congratulatory telegram to Minister Wang, and Minister Wang replied. The General Manager of the German Siemens Company sent a congratulatory telegram to Minister Wang, and Minister Wang replied. All workers and telegraphers of the International Radio Station sent a telegram to the Ministry of Communications (not translated and published).

Radio Station Communication: Yesterday, the communication that began to be implemented was the Sino-American Radio Station, which had been developed since 8:00 AM with extremely good results. All people from all walks of life who went to the station to send telegrams yesterday were not charged a fee. For fear of crowding, the number was limited to 1,000. After the initial reporting, the US side first responded with President Hoover's congratulatory telegram, which was openly displayed in the reporting room in good order.

Shipping Association Protests Japanese Inland River Navigation Rights

Please Expedite the Central Government's New Treaty

The Shanghai Shipping Association telegraphed Nanjing on the 5th, presenting to the Central Party Department, the National Government's Executive Yuan, and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of Communications, stating: The foreign encroachment on our country's inland river navigation rights is truly a legacy of unequal treaties. Fortunately, there is an awakening above and below, and a consensus to prepare to recover the restrictions of the past decades will soon be lifted. However, among foreigners, the most prominent who harbor aggressive ambitions and are unwilling to give up easily are our eastern neighbors, the Japanese. Therefore, they spare no effort in scheming and plotting, devising various strategies in an attempt to retain the rights they have already seized. Last year, there was a discussion between our country and their country to revise the new treaty. They once used the principle of reciprocity to lure us, but it was met with extreme opposition from our government and people. The Association also issued a declaration to state the advantages and disadvantages and express our determination. Although the discussion was suspended, a year has passed, and the new treaty has not yet been negotiated. Whether the right of navigation can be recovered is still at a critical juncture in a precarious situation. Now, reading the November 21st newspaper report on the remarks of the president of the Japanese Chamber of Commerce after returning to Shanghai, one section states: The Japanese Chamber of Commerce in China has proposed that the right of inland river navigation is related to the lifeline of Japanese merchants. I have tried my best to run around and lobby, and have received the strongest assistance from the authorities of the Ministry of Communications and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The most helpful are the leaders of the Japan-China Association and the directors of the Asia Bureau, etc. This shows that their country's officials and businessmen are working together with all their strength without the slightest slackness on this matter. The members of the Association were shocked and alarmed upon hearing this news, worrying about the past. Therefore, after discussion by the Executive Committee, there was a resolution to submit a request for attention. I dare to telegraph and appeal, hoping that you will pay attention during the negotiation of the new treaty, adhere to the principle of recovering lost navigation rights, and persevere until the goal is achieved, so as to comfort the public and protect national rights. I dare to make this statement and humbly ask for your attention and instruction. I cannot express my expectations enough. The Shanghai Shipping Association bows and sings.

Recent Plunge in Silver Prices

Foreign Press Says Gold Exchange Must Be Closed

The Great American Evening Post says: Foreign bankers in this port have been silent about the recent fall in the silver market. Today (the 6th), their bank managers broke their silence and denounced those who trade in gold as commoners of Jiujiang Road, pointing out that the current plunge in silver prices is caused by these people. It is said that although China has recently sought assistance in silver prices, saying that countries restrict the sale of silver, these Chinese at the Gold Exchange are still allowed to squeeze into the market to seek personal gain. As a result, a few people have become rich, while the national industry and commerce have suffered great harm. Without these people manipulating the market, foreign exchange could be sustained for a long time, and silver prices would not have fallen so drastically. Therefore, for the benefit of the entire country, the Gold Exchange should be closed. These Jiujiang Road people have been doing bullish trading in gold bars, gold coins, and Japanese gold in recent days, weakening the silver market and harming others to seek their own benefit. Among them, the most affected are the legitimate merchants engaged in import and export trade. As a result, the price of silver in New York fell by 2% on Thursday, and China was affected by this. Before Thursday, the market was thriving and becoming stable, and people were optimistic. After these Jiujiang Road people manipulated it, the phenomenon of today occurred. Therefore, these speculators who specialize in margin trading and gambling in buying and selling short have caused great harm to commerce and the country. These people often squeeze the silver market to seek their own profit. Today, for the sake of the Chinese government, it is urgent to prohibit them. Closing the exchange is the only way to save the situation today, it is said.

After detailed discussion by the committee members, it was decided to immediately telegraph the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to find ways to ask the group to pay attention to this matter and for the committee members to take the opportunity to speak at banquets hosted by various organizations in Shanghai.

Dexing Wheel Aground at Xindi

ChengSheng Ship Rescue Ineffective

62nd Regiment Changes Ship to Yue

Wanshou Wheel Collaterally Damaged

The water level in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River has decreased greatly recently, making navigation for merchant ships very difficult. Groundings and accidents are common. The Sanbei Company's Dexing wheel in this port was reported by telegram yesterday to have suffered damage due to grounding in the upper reaches of the river. The original report of this matter is as follows:

Sailing to Yuezhou The Sanbei Dexing wheel was leased by the Transportation Office on November 29th to transport the entire 62nd Regiment of the 11th Division, officers, soldiers, and military supplies to Yuezhou for landing and orders. In total, there were about 2,000 armed comrades in the entire regiment. After boarding the ship in Beijing, they proceeded to the upper reaches of the river, and it was expected that they could reach their destination at noon on the 2nd of this month.

Aground at Xindi The wheel, carrying soldiers upstream to Hunan, did not stop at Hankou, but went straight to Yuezhou. By the 2nd of this month, it was approaching Xindi, about ten Chinese miles away. It happened that the water was receding upstream, and the tide was only eight or nine feet high at high tide and only six or seven feet high at low tide. Dexing needed eleven feet of draft, so the ship was grounded as it passed through the area. Moreover, because there were 2,000 people and various military supplies on the wheel, the weight was even greater, and the wheel was stuck in the sand and mud and could not move at all.

Navy Rescue After the Dexing wheel was grounded, the shipowner repeatedly tried to reverse the wheel, but could not get out. The shipowner, unable to escape, urgently sent a wireless request for help. Fortunately, the Chengsheng warship was anchored there and received the distress call. It immediately sailed to the rescue. The Chengsheng warship took the Dexing and opened at full speed to tow it to the center of the river, but it did not move at all. Then, they waited until high tide before towing again, but still could not escape. The depth of the grounding is evident.

Transfer Ship For Transhipment The Chengsheng warship exhausted its efforts for the day, but could not rescue the Dexing. The officers and soldiers on board were anxious to reach the Yuezhou defense area and could not stay for long. The shipowner and the captain of the Chengsheng warship discussed and telegraphed Hankou to transfer the shallow-draft Wanshou and Wanli wheels to Xindi. Using the method of drawing wood from under the cauldron, all the officers, soldiers, and ordnance on the wheel were ordered to be transshipped by the two wheels to Yuezhou first, so as not to delay military operations, and at the same time, to reduce Dexing's load and make it easier to tow out.

Hull Damaged The Shanghai Bureau only received a telegram yesterday stating that the Dexing wheel had transferred all the soldiers and ordnance on board by two ships and had been sailing to Yuezhou for more than a day. After Dexing lightened its draft, it was only rescued from the shallows for the second time during high tide. The hull was damaged a lot and is under investigation. After the investigation, another loss list will be sent to Shanghai for verification. It is now planned to tow it back to Hankou or directly to Shanghai for major repairs. The Wanshou is also Damaged According to the report, the Wanshou shallow-draft wheel, which transported the officers and soldiers to Yuezhou, also struck the beach when it left the shallows, and also rammed into the outer hull of the Dexing. Therefore, the Wanshou wheel's hull was also damaged, but it did not prevent it from sailing. It is now necessary to wait until it arrives in Yuezhou and unloads the officers and soldiers before returning to Hankou to investigate the details and report separately.

Xingshi Engine Damaged The bureau also has the Jianglun Xingshi, which was temporarily rented by the chairman to inspect the Yangtze River and suppress the bandits, and Jiangtian, Fulong Yongxing Guupu, Dexing, and Jiangxin and other boats. They were used to transport troops and headquarters personnel to Jiangxi, Hubei, and Hunan provinces for bandit suppression. Now, the boats have been carrying soldiers upstream. The Xingshi was originally scheduled to transport soldiers to the west at the same time, but suddenly the engine in the wheel was damaged, preventing it from sailing. Yesterday, the shipowner urgently telegraphed the Shanghai Bureau to quickly transport machinery and materials, as well as hot and cold water pipe, and asked to send ship repair technicians and workers to Beijing to repair the ship.

Resolutions of the Pawn Industry Workers' Conference

Party Representatives Strenuously Prevent Work Stoppage

The Daily News reports that the citywide pawn industry workers held a representative assembly at the workers' union on the night of the day before yesterday at 9:00 PM. Over 100 representatives from various districts attended. Zhang Yaoming, a representative from the city party headquarters, was present to provide guidance. Cheng Tianzhai was publicly elected as chairman, and Deng Dunli recorded the proceedings. The chairman reported that the workers' union had submitted a request to the employers on July 31st of this year to revise the terms of worker treatment. The Social Bureau had set a deadline for labor and management to resolve the matter peacefully, but the employers had not sent a representative to negotiate. After the chairman's report, the party representative provided guidance, and then the proposals were discussed. It was resolved that all pawn industry workers in the city would unanimously engage in a work stoppage and petition the city party headquarters, the municipal government, and other institutions. However, the date of the work stoppage would be decided by a majority of the members. Thereupon, the city party representative, Zhang Yaoming, repeatedly advised and strenuously tried to prevent the strike. He argued that, regardless of the circumstances, the date of the work stoppage should be postponed for a few days to allow him to report back to the city party executive committee, which would then instruct the Social Bureau to make a final mediation. If, within this short period, the employers still lacked sincerity and mediation failed, then the workers could proceed with the work stoppage and petition. The representatives then decided to implement the work stoppage and petition the following Friday. However, they still hoped that the employers would implement revisions to the terms before the work stoppage to avoid a wave of strikes.

Red Cross Received Disaster Report from Huayin Yesterday

The Chinese Red Cross Society received a disaster report from Huayin, Shaanxi yesterday, the situation is particularly concerning and urgently disclosed as follows: Huayin is a barren and impoverished region with complicated and heavy taxation. During the Qing Dynasty, it supported passing troops and provided coolie labor to Beijia County (as the telegraph code reads). In years of good harvest, it also relied on Beijia County for grain supplies. After the reforms, coolie labor stopped. The grain supply for the Tongguan troops has never been sufficient. Therefore, eastern troops and coolies bear the brunt in Huayin, directly transporting supplies to Chang'an. Those coming from the west must change vehicles and horses in Huayin and send them east to the railway station. The annual transportation costs are often two to three hundred thousand, and the intangible losses from missing personnel and horses are even more incalculable. If we only consider the grain supply, the amount collected annually for the large army stationed in Tongguan, which is connected to the east, exceeds the regular maintenance costs by more than ten times. It is estimated that during the nineteen years, the grain supply for troops and coolies amounted to nearly twenty million yuan. The most impoverished areas bear this huge burden. Furthermore, years of military campaigns, famine, conscription, unwarranted levies, murder, arson, floods, droughts, windstorms, and locust plagues – every natural and man-made disaster has reached its limit. The income from a year of diligent labor is not enough to support the military and coolie expenses, and the legacies left by generations of ancestors are not enough to meet the demands. Bandits are like combs, soldiers are like rakes, and officials are like . The rich become poor, and the poor die. The dead cannot be brought back to life, and the living are left helpless and waiting for death. Markets are desolate, and villages are in ruins. Now that the overall situation has been settled, the surviving remnants can once again see the light of day. The weeds that harm the seedlings are about to be removed, and the fish stranded in ruts urgently await the river's nourishment. Therefore, we weep and earnestly plead for special grace and large amounts of funds to be quickly bestowed to rescue the afflicted people. It is hoped that the widespread cries of distress will have some effect. In our haste, we may be speaking carelessly. We humbly implore your consideration.

Representatives of the disaster-stricken people of Huayin: Wang Chongqing, Yuan Shuming, Shi Jingren, Jing Yizhai, all bowing and weeping.

Patrol Vessels Outside Songkou Vigorously Suppress Pirates

Intercepted a Pirate Ship

Killed More Than a Dozen Pirates

Rescued More Than Thirty Hostages

Now Sent to Kanmen for Disposal

The Gong Sheng patrol vessel of the Wusong National Coastal Defense Headquarters was patrolling the waters outside Wusongkou on the afternoon of the day before yesterday at approximately 5:00 PM when it suddenly spotted five pirate ships approaching rapidly in the distance in the waters off Jinshan Island. The vessel immediately pursued and engaged them. Unexpectedly, the pirate ships, upon seeing the patrol vessel approach, also opened fire and surrounded and attacked the vessel. The captain of the vessel, Wan Shaoxian, seeing the unfavorable situation, ordered the opening of machine guns and rapid-firing cannons. The pirates' momentum faltered, and they sailed away. The vessel pursued and intercepted a five-masted pirate ship on the spot, killing more than a dozen pirates. The rest fled into the water. More than thirty hostages, both male and female, young and old, were rescued. Four other pirate ships escaped due to darkness and rough seas. Yesterday, Captain Wan telegraphed the Coastal Defense Headquarters to report the defeat of the pirates. Director Wu reported that the intercepted pirate ship was reportedly a Fujianese merchant ship that had been seized by pirates near Beiguan. Therefore, Captain Wan sent the ship and the rescued hostages to Chairman Li of the Kanmen Chamber of Commerce for collection and distribution.

Fictitious Business Names Used to Defraud Large Amounts of Goods

Twenty-Nine Victims

Worth 38,000 Yuan

Case Solved in Changshu

Detectives Will Escort Suspects and Recover Goods

Shen Ziqing, a native of Shaoxing, fraudulently established three companies with fictitious names at Shandong Road and Wuhu Road in this municipality, and defrauded twenty-nine businesses, including Longhua Silk Factory, of goods worth 38,000 yuan. The case has been solved in Changshu, and seven large boxes of stolen goods have been recovered. The Zhabei Police Station has ordered detectives to go to Changshu to escort the suspects and recover the goods. The details of the investigation are as follows:

Setting up Companies with False Names In the autumn of this year, three companies with the names Fengtian Shen Zhuang suddenly appeared in this municipality. One was Hengxingde, located on Shandong Road in Wuma Road, and the others were Yongliren and Yongyihe, both located above the Tongshun Gong Warehouse on Wuhu Road. The managers of the three companies were all Cao Wenfu (actually Shen Ziqing's alias), and the internal accountants were Tao Heming (Shen's brother-in-law) and Xu Yaoting. They specialized in trading silk, foreign goods, and cosmetics. Initially, when purchasing goods from various merchants, they paid in cash. During the second transaction, they would owe half of the payment, promising to pay it on a specific date, and then they would pay on time to build trust with the factories. The factories also believed that Hengxingde and the other two shops did exist in Fengtian, so they trusted Shen even more when he purchased goods. Unexpectedly, in the final transaction, they did not pay at all.

The Discovery of the Fraudulent Scheme On the 27th of last month, Shen had taken goods worth over 10,000 yuan from Longhua Silk Factory in the name of Hengxingde. When the payment date arrived, Zhu Ganqing, a salesman from Longhua, went to Hengxingde to collect the payment and saw that Shen had absconded and all the goods in the shop had been moved away. Only a shop assistant, Pu Yousheng, had not left. He discovered Shen's alias and realized that they had been defrauded. Upon questioning, Pu Yousheng said that Shen had gone to Shen Jinzhang's place in Hongqiao, Zhabei. He tracked them there and found the goods were indeed there, but the two Shen's were nowhere to be found. He immediately reported to the local court and asked the Zhabei Police Station to arrest the suspects and recover the goods.

Victimized Businesses News of the fraud spread, and it was learned that the two companies, Yongliren and Yongyihe, had also collapsed, leaving only empty houses. Those who were defrauded included Tongming Electrical Material Factory, Zhenhua Weaving Factory, Hongyuan Silk and Satin Factory, Xu Jinji Huzhou Silk Factory, Meixin Silk Gauze Factory, Tongchang Sock Factory, Yusheng, Xiji, Sida, Jingda and other silk factories, Yitaifeng, Taifeng, Siyi, Longhua Silk Factory, Huitong, Yongyuan, Yixin Toothbrush Factory, Anda Cloth Factory, Yixingtai, Sanmin, Shengxin, Yuansheng, Hongda, Zhenhe Cloth Factory, Jiuyi, Zhida, Fuchengxiang, Yongfa, Wang Rongji - twenty-nine businesses in total, with a total value of 38,000 yuan.

Arrest and Recovery of Goods Detective You A'gen of the Zhabei Police Station learned from Pu Yousheng, a shop assistant at Hengxingde, that Shen had sent two boxes of goods to Changshu before absconding, but the address was not detailed. He sent a letter to Xu Fengshan, the Shanghai-based detective captain stationed in Changshu, Suzhou, to investigate. Captain Xu, along with detectives Yang Baokang and Chen Guangcai, went to Yu, Changshu and joined forces with Zhu Shunqing, the captain of the local detective team. They captured Tao Heming at the Yinlou Association in Sangjia Lane and recovered nine boxes of goods. Two of the boxes were empty, and seven of them were filled with towels, undershirts, toothbrushes, soap, and other stolen goods.

Escorting the Suspects Back to Justice Upon questioning, Tao Heming denied colluding with Shen Ziqing to commit fraud, claiming that Shen owed him money, so he went to Shanghai to seize his goods as compensation. He claimed that he had entrusted relatives Qian Zhongchun and Chen Zhongqing to introduce and deposit the boxes at the Yinlou Association. Tao and the stolen goods were temporarily detained at the local public security bureau pending extradition. It was reported that Tao had purchased ten yuan worth of straw to cover the boxes when transporting them to Changshu. Captain Xu and others have returned to Shanghai yesterday (the 6th) and informed the Zhabei Police Station to prepare a document to extradite the suspects and recover the goods. Zhu Ganqing is staying at the No. 1 Hostel outside Yanmen in Suzhou. It is heard that there are new developments in the case in Suzhou.

A Robbery of a Car by Bandits in the French Concession Last Night

The Car Was Rented from Zhapu Road

Driven to the French Concession and Robbed

The Driver Reported to the Police After Being Driven Out

Still Not Found by Midnight

At 8:55 last night, a dashing customer dressed in Western-style clothes, wearing a felt hat, and speaking with a local accent, who appeared to be around thirty years old, suddenly arrived at the Dalong Automobile Company at Nos. 136-138 Zhapu Road, Hongkou. He claimed to be named Chen Xianglin and said he needed to hire a car to drive around. The company's accountant heard this and, judging by his appearance, assumed he was a student and did not suspect anything. He immediately ordered the driver, Gu Jinbao (from Suzhou), to drive the No. 18117 (City No. 514) convertible car. The young man sat upright in the car and ordered the driver to drive to the French Concession. The driver started the engine and drove south. When the car reached the vicinity of Route Lafayette and Rue du Père Froc, the young man suddenly ordered the car to stop. As the car was still slowing down, two people suddenly emerged from the roadside, raised their hands to signal the young man, continued to board the car, drew out handguns, and forced the driver out of the car. The driver, intimidated by their force, was dragged out of the car, and one of the robbers drove off westward like a bat out of hell. The driver shouted for help to no avail and ran to the Louza Wan General Police Station to report the incident. The head of the police station, upon hearing the news, immediately informed the special agency to send detectives to investigate and used the telephone to notify all police stations in the Public Concession and the various district offices of the Chinese Public Security Bureau to be on the lookout for the car. However, the car had not been found by midnight, and no other incidents had been reported. It was also heard that the Dalong Automobile Company had also experienced a similar incident last autumn, when bandits rented a car near Fudan University and kidnapped a hostage.

Indian Policeman Accused of Disobedience

Interrogation at the British Consulate

The Shanghai Times reports that Indian policeman, Ka Tai Xin, was accused of distributing seditious texts with another Indian, Que Nan Xin. Yesterday (the 5th) the case was opened at the British Consulate's police court. Que Xin asked to reserve judgement, while Ka Tai Xin declared in court that it was amazing that they were requesting the government for rights and were now being accused of sedition. Ever since a foreign government ruled India, the blood and bones of the Indian people were being sucked. Such a government cannot be expected to bestow benevolence. The Indian people are being worn down by tyrannical rule and can no longer endure it. Today, they cry out loudly. The current authorities imprison three quarters of those who love their country and put in effort for their country. They are willing to accept any ruling, but the Indian people will inevitably use force to break the bonds of oppression. As long as they have a breath left, they will resist the government. It is noted that the two defendants are accused of distributing or spreading seditious printed material at the corner of Qiujiang Road and North Sichuan Road on the 25th. At the last hearing, one refused to face the judge and struggled with a Western police chief who forcibly turned him around. Neither defendant hired a lawyer and defended themselves. Que Nan Xin was later convicted of privately hiding weapons and sentenced to one month of imprisonment with hard labor. Another Indian named Tai La Xin was detained in the same case and sentenced to one week in prison and fined seven dollars and eight cents. The trial for the sedition charges for Ka Tai and Que were set to be continued at a later date.

Yang Tihwai's Tragic Death Was Actually Due to a Nervous Breakdown

Studied Diligently in France

Mental Faculties Weakened

It Can Be Said He Died for His Studies

Body Collected by Friends

Yang Tihwai from Rong County, Sichuan, studied at the University of Robechs, France and this year earned a bachelor's degree in textile engineering. He returned to China last month and first went to Beijing. Because traffic on the Pinghan Railway had not yet been restored, he detoured, planning to take a boat west from Shanghai. After arriving in Shanghai, he resided at the YMCA dormitory on Sichuan Road. At 4:15 PM the day before yesterday, he jumped out of the window from the fourth floor of the building where he was staying and was severely injured. He was sent to the hospital for treatment, as was reported in yesterday's newspaper. However, Yang's injuries were too severe, and he soon died. Upon receiving the report, the General Police Station dispatched Chinese detective Wu Junqing and Western detective to transport the body to the forensic laboratory on Ferren Road for examination. It was found that the deceased had no relatives in Shanghai. Only two friends, Wu Jialun and Tang Shicheng, currently managers at Ruita Ni Rong, No. 616 Nanjing Road, were found. Tang, a bachelor of engineering, met the deceased by chance during his journey back to the country. According to Wu, Yang's suicide was purely due to a nervous breakdown. Rumors that he was unemployed and took this action were false. Yang studied textile engineering very diligently in France, and his mental faculties became weakened. When his ship passed Taiwan on his way back from France, he had a major nervous breakdown. Therefore, when he arrived in Shanghai, this illness recurred, and he spoke deliriously, which resulted in this tragic incident. It can be said that he died for his studies. Yesterday morning, Guo Wei, a prosecutor from the Special District Local Court, arrived at the forensic laboratory for an examination. Wu Jialun claimed that he was willing to claim the body for coffin and burial. Magistrate Guo then instructed that Yang Tihwai's body be handed over to Wu for signing and collection for coffin and burial.

Extortion Within Extortion

The Case Is Extremely Bizarre and Worth Investigating

How Should Xue Bin Be Thoroughly Investigated?

Zhou Hesong, a local man, 31 years old, has been operating a redwood shop at No. 122 Huitongguan Street, Nantao, and his business has been relatively prosperous. Therefore, Zhou has some savings, which aroused the covetousness of bandits. For months, Zhou has been receiving four letters by mail, in which the senders claimed to be from a "dare-to-die team," demanding to "borrow" 1,000 yuan, or they would take drastic measures. The wording was extremely fierce. The last letter had reduced the amount to 300 yuan, instructing Zhou to wrap the money and send it to No. 71 Haichao Temple Road, outside Xiaonanmen, to be handed over to a man named Yao Baoshan at 5:30 PM yesterday. If he did not come, they would personally come to "welcome" him. After receiving these threatening extortion letters, Zhou immediately reported them to the First Precinct of the First District, requesting a thorough investigation and punishment. Upon receiving the notification, the Detective Team, led by Dong Mingde, the leader of the Nantao Precinct, along with detectives Yuan Haishan, Lu Anpu, Yu Maolong, Ren Shuzhi, Xu Yulin, and others, instructed Zhou's friend Zhu Jinde, a native of Shaoxing, to wrap fake banknotes and prepare them. Yesterday, they went to the address on time for negotiation. The detectives made their reconnaissance inside and outside the house. When Zhu took the money into the house and inquired, Yao Baoshan came out to meet him. The detectives immediately rushed in, arrested Yao, and took him back for questioning. Yao claimed that his name was Shan Bao, that he was 19 years old from Pinghu, and that his father's name was Yao Hanhou, who operated a rice shop at No. 34 Tangji Bridge in his hometown. He graduated from Yachuan Middle School and came to Shanghai this summer to study in the high school department of Junyi Middle School. He initially boarded at No. 6 Tiandeli near the school. One day, a woman came to talk to him, and they became quite friendly. She asked if he had a pillow, and he said he did not. She sent him a pillow the next day. Several days later, he noticed that her behavior was inappropriate, so he refused to let her come again. Unexpectedly, she still came from time to time. Unable to bear the harassment, he secretly moved to his classmate Lin's house at No. 71 Haichao Temple Road. Unexpectedly, she found out and came again. He scolded her and drove her away. She became angry and incited a group of hooligans to beat him up and extort money from him. Knowing he could not win, he was introduced to Xue Bin by a friend, Xu Qinghe. Xue mediated and had him pay 3 yuan to settle the matter. Xue had come to his place three or four times. Recently, he suddenly received a letter claiming that someone would send several packages of medicine cakes to him to be collected on their behalf. As a result, he was framed. He said that he did not know anything about the reasons, and he showed the original letter from Xue. The detectives carefully checked it and found that the handwriting was completely consistent with the threatening letters Zhou had received. Yao also claimed that Xue Bin practiced martial arts at the City No. 1 Martial Arts Hall and lived on Zhonghua Road in Xiaoximen. His father ran a machine factory. The detectives went to the address, but Xue Bin had already fled, only his mother, Mrs. Xue Yan, a native of Anhui, was arrested and brought back, and then sent to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

No Hope for Resolution in the Nanyang Medical College Dispute

President Adds Charges

Students Request Extension for Reconciliation

Nanyang Medical College President Wu Zongqing and the college's student union executive committee members Liu Zefu, Gao Changguo, Lu Yiqiu, and eight others had disagreements over school affairs, leading to mutual accusations and the hiring of lawyers at the Special District Local Court. After the court ordered them to go outside for reconciliation, as reported in the newspaper, it is now learned that the relationship between teachers and students at the college has reached a breaking point and cannot be repaired. Not only is reconciliation hopeless, but Wu Zongqing has now added charges, stating that Liu Zefu and others admitted in court during the last hearing that they had jointly invaded the school's office on November 5 and chased away teachers, falsely claiming to be maintaining school affairs. The investigation found that Liu and others had entered and taken over, damaged, and sealed off the office without the permission of the authorities, violating Article 317 of the criminal law. Furthermore, the defendants admitted in court that they were members of the student union and the maintenance association, so the rights and actions of the student union and the maintenance association should be the responsibility of Liu and others. Therefore, the plaintiff requested that the defendants be punished in accordance with the aforementioned articles of law and Article 118, paragraph 1, of the criminal law. Liu Zefu also requested the court to summon several professors from the school to prove that students were still attending classes normally on the morning of the 5th and that the order was good. He also requested that the officers of the maintenance association, Zheng Xiansheng, Guan Guanwu, Huang Qibai, and Chen Mingbo, as well as the detectives from the Gordon Road Police Station, be summoned to testify that the sealing of the safe was not done by Liu and others, but that Wu Zongqing instigated the arrest. Yesterday was the date for the continuation of the trial. The students' lawyer requested another postponement in order to seek a method of reconciliation, and Wu Zongqing's lawyer also agreed. Gao Changguo then stated in court that if there was a reconciliation, the court would have to resolve it. Judge Ge ordered that the hearing be held again on the afternoon of the 22nd of this month.

Continuation of the Case Against He Gengxing and Others

Awaiting Letter from the Zao Gong Temple for Investigation Before Retrial

He Gengxing, a compradore at Mitsui Yangxing, abandoned his job and absconded in May. At the same time, Hongyu and Huiyu, two hardware stores he opened on Tianzhu Tang Street in the French Concession, filed for bankruptcy with the French Public Concession. After sending an accountant to clear the accounts, He's creditors, Hengyu and eight other money shops and Zhengda Bank, sent representatives to the accountant's office to investigate the accounts and discovered evidence of collusion and fraud with He Junxing, Ma Changjia, Jin Youcheng, Jin Youzhang, and others. They hired lawyers Wang Fuchang and Yuan Hanyun to accuse He and the other four of jointly defrauding and taking property at the Special District Local Court. The summons was issued some days ago, but since the defendants had not all arrived, a new date was set, as was reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu Tingqi opened the court for the continuation of the trial. First, he asked the five defendants, He Gengxing and others, about their ages and addresses. Then, he questioned the plaintiff's representative, Wang Honglai. He said that this case arose because He requested bankruptcy, and that the Hongyu and Huiyu hardware stores were both located in the French Concession. He Gengxing also claimed to reside in the French Concession, and the bankruptcy was approved by the French Public Concession. Then why was the case not filed with the French Public Concession? The plaintiff's lawyer, Wang Fuchang, replied that this case differed from the one handled by the French Public Concession in three points: (1) the plaintiffs are different. Hengyu Money Shop was not involved in the accusation to the French Public Concession, but is now included. (2) The accused are different. The accusation to the French Concession only involved He Gengxing, but now includes He Junxing and the other four, and these four all live in the Public Concession. (3) The facts of the accusation are different. The accusation to the French Public Concession was that He Gengxing absconded with money, but now the defendants colluded to conceal property and harm the interests of the creditors. Furthermore, the French Public Concession is not a formal Chinese court, and according to Article 17 of the Litigation Regulations, related cases can be transferred to your court for handling. He Gengxing's lawyer, Wang Youling, refuted the points raised by the plaintiff's lawyer one by one, saying that the first point could not be established because a plaintiff could not be arbitrarily added to bring a case to another judicial organ. Secondly, He Gengxing was the defendant in the French Public Concession and is also the defendant in this case, and there is no such thing as being tried in two places. Thirdly, the accusation in the French Public Concession was that he violated Article 363 of the criminal law, and the same is true now. He requested that the portion of the accusation against He Gengxing be rejected. The lawyers for the other four defendants argued that the judicial organ where the incident occurred had jurisdiction over criminal cases. After the plaintiff's lawyers argued, the plaintiff's lawyer finally stated that He Gengxing's actual address was not in the French Concession, and that he had been accused by a Ningbo money shop in your court before. A review of the case file would reveal the truth. Judge Wu then ordered a letter to be sent to the Jian Public Concession to investigate the bankruptcy situation of Gengxing and the rest, and then to review the situation.

The Result of Free Love

Misunderstanding the Marriage Autonomy Law

Chen Mingqi Sentenced to Six Months in Prison

Lan Lianchen, who wrote the name card for Holland Yangxing and lived in Huajinpailou in the city, had a daughter named Lan Xufang. She studied at Ai Qun Girls' School and loved freedom. She had a free love relationship with Chen Mingqi, a handsome young man in Western clothes. Unexpectedly, her father betrothed Xufang to a wealthy Wen family in Nanxun last year. Lan Xufang was only nineteen years old last year and did not meet the marriage autonomy law, so she fled to the Women's Association for a year. This October, Chen discussed with Lan Xufang that Xufang was already 20 years old and had reached the age of marriage autonomy. In fact, she would not turn 20 until her birthday in March of next year. They misunderstood the law and hired a lawyer to rashly publish a marriage notice. At the same time, they held their overly free wedding at Ximenli, Ximen Road. As a result, Lan Lianchen angrily reported the incident to the police, and they were arrested and sent to the local court for investigation. They were prosecuted for enticing a woman under the age of twenty. Although Chen tried his best to argue that the woman agreed, the law states that those under the age of twenty are of weak will, so the crime was established. Yesterday morning, Court President Shen brought Chen to court and announced the verdict, sentencing him to six months in prison. He has been imprisoned. Lan Xufang has returned home with her father and is following her father's wishes.

The Fate of Chen Guibao: What is to Become of Her?

First Husband Poisoned

Second Husband Goes Mad

Chen Baokang, from the western countryside of Longhua, worked as a carpenter. He had a daughter named Guibao, aged 22. Two years ago, her uncle arranged for her to be betrothed to Jiang Erbao, the young owner of a tofu shop in Xujiahui. Last September, as the wedding date approached, Jiang Erbao contracted syphilis and died. This spring, a neighbor again acted as matchmaker, arranging for Guibao to marry a Mr. Lang who owned a barrel-making shop in Zhabei. The engagement took place in April of this year, and the Lang family had already chosen an auspicious date in November for the wedding. They asked the matchmaker to inform the Chen family. However, Chen received news that Mr. Lang had suddenly gone mad and was bedridden. Mr. Lang, knowing the wedding date was near and fearing he would be unable to marry as planned, discussed with the matchmaker a postponement until he fully recovered. Chen, upon learning this from the matchmaker, was very anxious, as madness is difficult to cure quickly. Guibao eventually learned the truth and questioned her father. Chen initially hid the truth, but after her persistent inquiries, he had to tell her. Guibao lamented her fate and told her father that she was destined for misfortune and would not marry, desiring to enter a nunnery instead. She asked her father to quickly dissolve the engagement with Mr. Lang. Her father, fearing that his daughter would become ill with worry, comforted her. On the 2nd of this month, Guibao, taking advantage of her family's inattention, took a small bundle and left home, never to return. Her parents were greatly alarmed when she did not return by evening and searched for her among their relatives, but all said she had not arrived. They became even more worried. For the past two days, her parents have been searching for her in the nunneries north and south of the city, but it is unknown whether they will find her.

A Mr. Zhang from Guangdong, who works in the Nanjing government and resides at No. 127 Sida Lane, Sigao Road, employed a 36-year-old female servant named Zhang Ding from Yangzhou. Her condition is reportedly critical.

Anti-Opium Society Urges Strict Investigation of Major Drug Trafficking Case

Fujian Organizations Petition for Investigation

The China National Anti-Opium Society, citing news from Geneva and reports in mainland newspapers on August 17th, stating that the British government had submitted a report to the League of Nations identifying Xiamen as a center for drug trafficking and Zhang Yongshun as a major drug trafficker, who was arrested at a station in Myanmar in September 1928 with ten cans of goods labeled as being produced in Germany, and it was found that this drug was commissioned by Xiamen physician Zhang Yongshun for purchase, and the rest was shipped to a business in London for transshipment elsewhere. According to the business, the goods were transported by the head office to Shanghai and then to Xiamen for physician Zhang Yongshun's use. Furthermore, in October of the same year, 32 taels of morphine, 500 taels of heroin, and 20 pounds of Persian opium were seized in Yangon. The heroin was also produced in Germany, under similar circumstances. This batch of drugs was also shipped to Xiamen Physician Zhang Yongshun. Among the aforementioned drugs, not only German heroin but also a large quantity of morphine bearing trademarks was intended to be sold through a British business, but the attempt failed due to the forged labels. In addition, 100 taels of heroin manufactured in Tokyo, Japan, along with 225 taels of heroin bearing the E. Merck trademark, were also seized at the same time. Based on these facts, the British government requested the League of Nations to protest to China. The Anti-Opium Society believes that Zhang Yongshun's drug trafficking harms the country, and his crime is unpardonable. Moreover, trafficking to Southeast Asia not only harms overseas Chinese but also damages the nation's reputation. Based on the facts presented by the British government, the society appealed to the Central Anti-Opium Committee. The committee then requested the Fujian Anti-Opium Committee to investigate. The Fuzhou and Xiamen authorities dispatched personnel to arrest the principal offender, but without success. It has been nearly two months, and the suspect is still at large. The various Fujian organizations have reported to the Anti-Opium Society, requesting continued efforts. Recently, the Xiamen Siming County Party Affairs Guidance Committee sent a letter advocating strict investigation and instructed local authorities to investigate. Furthermore, organizations such as the Shanghai Federation of All Circles and the Shanghai Fujian Student Association have advocated strict investigation to the Anti-Opium Society, and a joint meeting of various organizations has been held to resolve the issue of appealing to the government. In addition, the Chinese Pharmaceutical Society has advocated strict investigation of the use of these drugs. The Anti-Opium Society has followed the resolution of the General Assembly and requested the Central Anti-Opium Committee to investigate. Yesterday, it was reliably learned that the principal offender, Zhang Yongshun, is very influential and is using money to send his associates around to lobby in Beijing and Shanghai to avoid arrest. The society believes this case is as shocking as the Gao Yingtu case and has listed the facts to inform all parties to pay attention and unanimously advocate thorough resistance to emphasize drug prohibition and maintain national reputation.

Final Draft of "A Study of the Original Characters in Shuowen Jiezi" Completed

Compiled and Written by Xu Wancheng

Xu Wancheng (Shangyi) from Zhangyan, Jinshan, graduated from Daxia University and has served as a teacher at Wuxi National College, Taicang Middle School, Shanghai Nanyang Commercial School, Shanghai Lubein, and Suzhou Provincial Library. He currently teaches at Baoshan Junior High School. Based on Ding Fubao's "Shuowen Gulin," Xu has compiled "A Study of the Original Characters in Shuowen," which makes numerous corrections to common corrupted characters. This will be of great benefit to scholars. A Glimpse of the Shanghai Bank's Service to Society

The Shanghai Bank's Xiafei Road branch opened for business on the 15th of last month. Each morning, the branch posts the latest silver and stock market prices at its entrance. Residents of the French Concession who wish to know the overseas silver market fluctuations can conveniently visit the Xiafei Road branch located at No. 365, west of the Paris Cinema.

The Great Prosperity of the Daxin Silk and Satin Store After Winter Discounts

Since the winter discounts, the business of the Daxin Silk and Satin Store on Shilu Sanma Road has flourished, making it the leader in Shanghai's silk industry. It is reported that the store has commissioned various manufacturers to produce red cloud crepe, bear-squeeze crepe, goose-alarm crepe, kylin crepe, and printed maoge and velvet in various colors. As these goods continue to arrive in Shanghai, customers have been even more eager to purchase them. Daily sales have reached dozens of bolts.

Jiujiang Native Association Re-elects Officers

The Jiujiang Shanghai Native Association held its seventh annual meeting and elected new officers yesterday. Over a hundred members were present. Hua Chuanbao was elected chairman and Tan Wufu as secretary. After performing the necessary rituals, the chairman reported on the association's activities over the past year and discussed future development. Then, officers were elected. The Supervisory Committee members are Hua Chuanbao, Liu Haiquan, Zhu Zhaotang, and Zeng Fuxing. The Executive Committee members are Nie Xuntai, Wu Shixi, Liu Qingyu, Tan Wufu, Zhu Zerun, or Zhiwu, and Li Xianrong. The secretary is Wei Xinmin, the document keeper is Kongzi Zhen, the accountant is Zhou Hanzhang, the social contact is Gong Jiating, and the investigator is Liu Zhuqi.

Xu Zhijiang Arrives in Shanghai

Xu Zhijiang, commander of the Provisional Third Division of the First Advance Force of the Anti-Rebellion Army of the Land, Sea, and Air Force Headquarters, arrived in Shanghai yesterday on official business to purchase supplies. He received a telegram from Liu Yizhai, commander of the Advance Force, urging him to return to Zhengzhou quickly because an inspection is imminent. He will depart Shanghai as soon as his business is completed.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the Shandong area and the Yangtze River basin are cloudy. There is fog on the coast here. The wind direction is uncertain along the Chinese coast. The weather is bad around the Ogasawara Islands. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in Shanghai was 55.0 degrees and the lowest was 37.3 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 57.0 degrees and the lowest was 31.3 degrees.

Letter

To the Editor: According to Mr. He Shengdi, the person concerned, the article "House Dispute in Gujia Lane, Beijing Road" in today's news section of your esteemed newspaper is not factual. He asserts that although he was involved in a lawsuit with tenants at that location in 1923, the case was settled out of court and there was no requirement that the owner wait until 1933 to rebuild. The report is inaccurate. Please correct it as soon as possible. Sincerely, Jiang Yiping and Wu Baotai, Attorneys at Law, December 6, 1930.

To the Editor: In today's local news section of your esteemed newspaper, the news about the theft of firearms from the Yangjing Town Security Corps should state that the instructor Chen Hongsheng is a mistake for Chen Ruiqi, i.e., Xinmin. Please correct it. Sincerely, First Team of the Yangjing District Security Corps, Shanghai City, December 6, 1930.
